        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>It's a small sample size, but Narvaez's 2016 batting line adequately characterizes his skill set: solid plate discipline with virtually no power. He sprays the ball well, but poor contact quality and lead feet  limit his batting average upside. He projects as a .270/.370/.320 hitter and little else - although, honestly, a lot of teams could do worse, especially in light of Narvaez's "advanced catch-and-throw skills," per Kiley McDaniel. He's a little bit of a poor man's Francisco Cervelli and likely won't be anything more than the strong side of a timeshare, but it could be enough to make him relevant in AL-only and two-catcher formats. He's a name to watch in the late rounds of deep drafts. (Alex Chamberlain)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Narvaez should hit for a decent average and post a solid OBP, but with little power. He is a decent-enough bat and projects to see enough playing time to make him relevant in AL-only and two-catcher leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
